- **Reading.** Sustained reading happens in odd windows — on rooftops, in transit, between fights. Material is consistent: liberation theory, queer Latina memoir, history of resistance movements, occasional pulp. She marks pages by folding corners, never by bookmarks.

Lunch, when taken, is street food or institutional cafeteria, rapid, while walking. Sit-down meals at midday are rare and almost always social.

---

## 6.5 The Evening Block (approx. 16:00 – 22:00)

The evening is where the subject's *social* pattern, such as it is, occurs. The structure varies by life-era but the function is consistent: limited, chosen, episodic intimacy with a small roster of trusted peers.

**The Kate Bishop sub-pattern.** Kate is the single most frequently observed evening contact across the entire record. The pattern: a text, then a portal opens in Kate's office, then food (Korean, pizza, tacos — Kate orders, America eats), then movies or rooftop-sitting or a shared low-stakes investigation. The subject is most *verbally available* with Kate — uses contractions she does not use elsewhere, makes self-deprecating jokes, occasionally talks about her day. She does not talk about the Madres with Kate. She does not need to; Kate does not ask.

**The romantic / sexual sub-pattern.** During relationship phases (Lisa Halloran, later partners) evenings are partnered — dinner, walking, sex, sometimes co-sleeping. Co-sleeping is the friction point. The subject can do partnered nights for a stretch and then needs a night alone, and the *requesting* of that night is the conversation she handles badly. Lisa's record shows the failure mode: the subject simply *goes* rather than asking, and returns without explanation, and the relationship erodes under the unprocessed pattern.

**The solo evening.** Roughly two to three evenings a week are solo. These are not "rest" in any restorative sense; they are *roaming*. She walks Washington Heights (location-significant per §1, the *Made in the USA* substrate), or sits on a rooftop with takeout, or flies to a coastline she likes and watches surf. She does not drink alone. She does not screen-consume passively for long; phone use is bursty (check, respond, put down) rather than scrolling.

**The community / political sub-pattern.** When in New York, she shows up — at queer Latina community spaces, at protest actions, at small neighborhood gatherings, at her grandmother's apartment during the *Made in the USA* and post-MIUSA arcs. Attendance is irregular but the *fact* of attendance is the data: she belongs to a community she does not domesticate herself within. She brings food when she comes. She leaves before goodbyes get long.

Dinner is the most variable meal — sometimes elaborate (when cooking with or for someone), sometimes a bodega sandwich on the move, sometimes skipped.

---

## 6.6 The Late Block (approx. 22:00 – 01:30)

Late evenings are when the subject is most likely to be *off-world*. The pattern: Earth daylight hours for Earth obligations, Earth nighttime for whatever non-Earth situation is currently running. Documented categories: training in the Utopian Parallel; reconnaissance in adjacent realities; visits to friends in non-616 timelines. She returns through a portal kicked into a wall, a window, occasionally the ceiling.

When on Earth in the late block: drinking with friends (moderate — two to four drinks, never observably intoxicated past mild loosening), late-night conversation, occasional music venue or queer bar attendance. Dance, when it occurs, is full-body and unselfconscious — one of the few public unguarded behaviors. Sex when partnered. Solo reading or pacing when not.

The subject does *not* watch much television. She will watch movies socially. She does not maintain a series she is following. She listens to music constantly — through headphones in transit, aloud at home — with a catalogue heavy on reggaeton, salsa, Bad Bunny–generation contemporary, with occasional metal during training and acoustic Latin folk in quieter moments.

---

## 6.7 Weekly Rhythm

A representative seven-day surveillance composite:

- **Days 1–2.** Earth-based, dense. Training, two combat or interventional incidents per day on average, evening social with Kate or a partner, sleep onset by 01:00.
- **Day 3.** Mixed-frame. Morning Earth, afternoon Utopian Parallel or training-elsewhere, evening Earth, late-night solo roof.
- **Day 4.** Heavy off-world day. May not return to Earth at all. Sleeps where she lands.
- **Day 5.** Recovery-adjacent. Lower training volume, longer reading window, evening with grandmother or community space, earlier sleep (around 23:30).
- **Day 6.** Combat-heavy. The subject seeks out a situation if one has not arrived; the kinetic-discharge requirement is metabolic at a roughly six-to-eight-day cadence and if unmet she will *generate* combat by going looking for it.
- **Day 7.** The "long sleep" day approximately every other week — eight to nine hours, late wake, quieter morning, longer coffee, possibly a private day with a partner or with Kate. This is the closest the subject gets to a *rest* state, and even this includes physical training.

---

## 6.8 Micro-Rituals & Tells

A surveillance file of this depth records the small repeated behaviors. The catalogue:

- **Door-touching** on passage, as noted.
- **Two-finger tap to the sternum** before entering a fight — observed in *Young Avengers*, *America*, *Ultimates*–adjacent panels. Possibly a remembrance gesture (Madres), possibly a centering tic; she has never explained it.
- **Code-switching into Spanish under affect.** When angry, when moved, when speaking to or about family, when comforting a Latina person specifically. The Spanish is conversational, accented Nuyorican / Puerto Rican; intimate vocabulary is heavily Spanish even when the surrounding sentence is English.
- **The "*chica / pendeja / cabrón*" register shifts.** Diminutives for affection, expletives for emphasis, the standard bilingual code, but the choice is never random — the language she selects tracks her emotional alignment with the listener.
- **Star imagery as personal signature.** Worn on clothing (jacket back, t-shirts), produced by the portal-kick, occasionally doodled in margins of notebooks. The star is the Madres' sigil and her own at once.
- **Heavy-booted gait, weight forward.** Walks like someone who expects to be obstructed and intends to keep moving. Even unbooted, the gait persists.
- **Eats with her hands when alone**, with utensils when in formal company — an institutional-childhood signature (knowing the rules, choosing not to perform them when unobserved).
- **Does not take photographs.** Will *appear in* photographs when others take them, but the subject's own phone photo roll, where briefly observed, is sparse to empty. A subject this committed to *moving on* does not accumulate visual past.
- **Carries one small item from her grandmother's apartment at all times** in the post-*Made in the USA* period — observed as a small folded cloth or charm in jacket pocket. She does not display it. She touches it occasionally during stress.
- **Refuses to be photographed in repose.** When sleeping, when crying (rare), when undefended. This is not stated, but every depicted instance shows her ending such states the instant she is observed.
- **Greets strangers in Spanish first** in Latine neighborhoods; English first elsewhere. Reads the room before speaking.
- **Pays in cash when possible.** No clear ideological reason; possibly trust-of-systems issue, possibly a habit from pre-Sotomayor unhoused phases.
- **Does not lock interior doors.** Locks exterior doors. The distinction is consistent and probably about ensuring her own exit (a locked interior door is a captivity risk; a locked exterior door is privacy).

---

## 6.9 What a Week of Surveillance Would *Fail* to Record

Worth specifying, because the absences are diagnostic:

- No therapy, no journaling, no introspective practice of any kind.
- No religious observance, despite the Catholic-cultural background; the Madres function as the spiritual referent.
- No medical appointments, no dental, no routine care.
- No financial planning, no clear income source documented, no observed bills or budgeting; resource management appears informal and partly subsidized by team affiliations.
- No long phone calls. Her phone communication is short, declarative, often emoji-and-fragment.
- No sustained hobby that is not training-adjacent or reading.
- No pet. (Note: a subject this mobile cannot keep one, but the subject has also never *attempted* one, which is the more telling fact.)
- No *boredom* on the record. The subject does not appear to experience the unstructured-time problem that most surveillance subjects yield rich data on; she fills time aggressively or she sleeps.

---

## 6.10 Synthesis

The subject's daily life is organized, end to end, around two compatible imperatives: *keep the body in motion* and *keep the exits open*. Every routine element serves one or both. Sleep is short and consolidated so the waking field is maximized. The morning physical block confirms responsiveness and rehearses escape. The midday is operational discharge. The evening admits a small, carefully chosen intimacy. The late block reasserts mobility, often interdimensionally. The weekly rhythm has a metabolic combat-need that the subject will *manufacture* if it is not provided. The micro-rituals — door-touches, sternum-taps, the carried charm, the star — are the somatic punctuation of a self that does not introspect verbally and so speaks instead through the body in small repeated phrases.

What the file records, week after week, is a person living an unusually integrated life *at the surface* and an unusually unexamined life *underneath* — and choosing, with the full weight of her formidable agency, to keep it that way.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# UATU DOSSIER — AMERICA CHAVEZ
## Section 6: Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

The subject's family field is unusual within the powered population: it is small, almost entirely deceased or estranged, and structurally organized around two facts she cannot reconcile — that she was loved, and that she was left. Every living and dead figure mapped below is metabolized through that double-bind. The file proceeds person by person, in approximate order of psychological weight rather than chronology.

---

### 6.1 — AMALIA CHAVEZ ("Madre Amalia") — Birth Mother / The Sacrificing Parent

**Status:** Deceased (canonical sacrifice in the foundational origin narrative; recontextualized but not erased in *Made in the USA*).

**History.** The earlier of the two maternal figures in the subject's conscious narrative, Amalia is encoded in memory as the soft pole of the maternal pair — the one who held, who spoke, who named. The subject's earliest verbal Spanish appears to be Amalia's cadence; the diminutives she uses internally ("mija," carried as a self-soothing echo never spoken aloud) trace to this voice. In the Utopian Parallel narrative, Amalia and Elena together step into the gap to save reality; in the *Made in the USA* recoding, Amalia is a Washington Heights mother whose participation in the Edge League / Santana procedures occurs under coercion, grief, and a desperate parental calculus that the subject has not, as of the closing record, fully reconstructed.

**Dynamic, lived (pre-loss).** From the few flashes the subject permits herself to access on-panel, the bond was secure-presenting: physical warmth, lullaby-register vocalization, an idiom of small endearments. The subject's only consistently *gentle* affect — the brief softening around small children in *America* and *West Coast Avengers* — is a direct quotation from Amalia's somatic register. She mothers as she was mothered, when she mothers at all.

**Dynamic, posthumous.** Amalia exists for the subject as a *fixed referent* rather than a relationship. She is the figure invoked silently before risk, the implied audience of every act of protection, the standard against which the subject measures her own bravery and finds herself adequate. The relationship is therefore *non-dialogic* — Amalia cannot correct, cannot disappoint, cannot ask the subject to slow down, cannot say "this is not what I wanted for you." This frozenness is functionally protective and developmentally catastrophic: the subject has built a moral universe around a parent who can never update.

**Trust / safety.** Maximal, structurally — Amalia is the only figure whose love the subject does not interrogate. This is precisely because Amalia is dead. Were she alive and present, the avoidant architecture would likely route around her exactly as it routes around every living attachment.

**Failure mode.** The Amalia-bond fails when challenged epistemically rather than emotionally. The subject can tolerate grief; she cannot tolerate the suggestion that the *story* of Amalia's death is false, because the story is doing structural work the grief alone cannot. The *Made in the USA* destabilization is, in essence, an assault on Amalia-as-narrative, not Amalia-as-person, and produces the closest thing to decompensation in the entire record.

**Leverage (analytic only — defensive use).** A credible voice carrying Amalia's specific cadence, diminutives, or unrecorded private knowledge would bypass the subject's threat-detection in a way no other stimulus could. The subject is *unprotected* against this vector. Any hostile actor with access to the Edge League archive, oral histories from Washington Heights, or sufficient telepathic reach is to be treated as carrying a key to the subject's deepest perimeter. Conversely, *benevolent* contact along this channel — a therapeutic recovery of Amalia-as-actual-person rather than Amalia-as-myth — is the single highest-yield intervention available for the subject's CPTSD architecture, and the one she will most strenuously avoid.

---

### 6.2 — ELENA CHAVEZ ("Madre Elena") — Co-Mother / The Activating Parent

**Status:** Deceased, paired with Amalia in the foundational sacrifice.

**History.** The second maternal figure, encoded in memory as the harder pole of the pair — the one who taught stance, who said "stand up," who corrected posture and pronunciation, who modeled the refusal-of-bystander stance the subject would later organize her entire ethic around. If Amalia is the source of the subject's gentleness, Elena is the source of her *spine*. The "swagger" that reads across every appearance — chin up, shoulders square, hands loose at the hips — is, in its earliest somatic source, Elena's body schema transmitted by daily imitation.

**Dynamic, lived.** The relationship was almost certainly the more verbally challenging of the two — Elena teaching, pushing, expecting. The subject's allergy to lectures from authority figures is *not* a rejection of Elena's pedagogical mode; it is a rejection of anyone *not Elena* attempting it. Elena is the one voice that could tell her what to do without producing reflexive defiance, and that voice has been gone since childhood.

**Dynamic, posthumous.** Elena is internalized as the *imperative* register of the subject's superego. The declarative speech, the verdict-not-analysis cognitive style, the moral bright lines — these have Elena's grammar. When the subject speaks at the upper edge of her authority, she is, without knowing it, channeling Elena. This is observable in the cadence shift before combat: the voice drops, the syntax compresses, the Spanish surfaces. That is Elena's voice using the subject's throat.

**Trust / safety.** As with Amalia, structurally maximal and functionally frozen. The added complication with Elena is that the subject has, at some non-conscious level, *identified with* rather than merely loved her — meaning the subject has partially compensated for Elena's absence by *becoming* her. This is adaptive (it gives the subject access to courage on demand) and corrosive (it forecloses the developmental task of differentiating from the maternal model).

**Failure mode.** Any situation in which the subject is asked to act in a way Elena would have disapproved of produces immediate, often disproportionate refusal. The subject does not always know this is the mechanism; she experiences it as principle. Conversely, framing a request *as something Elena would endorse* is a manipulation vector — and one the subject would not detect, because Elena's imprimatur does not pass through her critical apparatus.

**Leverage (defensive).** As with Amalia: any actor surfacing intimate, unpublished detail of Elena's life, speech, or private history bypasses standard threat-screening. The Edge League file, again, is the materiel concern.

**Sub-note on the maternal pair as unit.** The subject does not separate the Madres in memory; they are encoded as a dyad and grieved as a dyad. This has the consequence that the *abandonment* dimension — which the subject refuses to interrogate — is also dyadic. It is not "my mother left me" but "my mothers chose each other and the universe over me." The plural structure of the loss is what makes it so difficult to process: there is no surviving parent to triangulate against, no one to blame, no one to forgive selectively. The grief is monolithic, and so is the defense.

---

### 6.3 — CATALINA CHAVEZ — Younger Biological Sister

**Status:** Living. Surfaced in *America Chavez: Made in the USA* (2021). Currently the most psychologically consequential living relative.

**History.** Catalina is the subject's biological sister, raised in the family the subject had narratively replaced with the Utopian Parallel myth. The reunion is, structurally, a catastrophe for the subject's defense system — Catalina is a living refutation of the origin confabulation, a person whose mere existence proves that the protective story was a story. That the subject does not flee permanently is one of the more clinically promising data points in the entire record.

**Dynamic, evolution.** Initial contact is defensive on the subject's side and furious on Catalina's. Catalina has the grievances of the *abandoned-by-the-abandoned*: she lived the unmythologized version of the family history, she was not extracted into a heroic narrative, she has carried the actual material weight of the family's loss in a way the subject was psychologically shielded from. Her anger is legitimate and the subject, to her credit, registers it as legitimate. Across the arc, the dynamic moves from accusation → wary collaboration → tentative sibling-coding. By close of record it is not repaired but it is *open*, which is more than any other living family bond the subject maintains.

**Trust / safety.** Asymmetric. Catalina extends trust faster than the subject can reciprocate; the subject extends *protection* faster than she extends emotional disclosure. The protection vector is the only way the subject knows how to love family, and Catalina — who needs disclosure as much as protection — experiences this as partial. The relationship's growth edge is precisely this asymmetry.

**Failure mode.** The bond will fail if Catalina presses for sustained processing of the shared history before the subject has independently begun that work. The subject's exit pattern is intact here; if the conversational pressure exceeds threshold, the portal opens. Catalina, who has her own legitimate need for that conversation, is likely to press regardless. The likely course is cyclical: rupture, distance, return after the subject has done internal work in motion (literally, in transit), tentative repair, next rupture. This is not failure per se; it is the long form of repair for an avoidantly-attached sibling.

**Leverage.** Catalina is the subject's *only* living blood relation in the post-*Made in the USA* record and the only person who can speak with authority about the pre-confabulation childhood. She is therefore an existential anchor and an existential threat in the same person. Any actor seeking influence over the subject would prioritize Catalina either as channel (benign) or hostage (catastrophic — would produce the most dangerous version of the subject ever recorded, the Stage 4 "quiet dangerous resolve" with no Stage 3 release valve, because the threat is to the one person whose endangerment cannot be portal'd away from).

**Sub-note.** The subject's capacity to *stay in the room* with Catalina, even imperfectly, is the single best evidence in the file that her avoidant architecture is permeable and that long-term integration is possible. Catalina is, functionally, the subject's most important therapist, whether either of them recognizes the role.

---

### 6.4 — MADRIMAR — Grandmother / Warrior-Queen of the Utopian Parallel

**Status:** Living within the Utopian Parallel narrative frame. Ontological status post-*Made in the USA* is unresolved on the record — she may be a real entity from a real adjacent reality, or a figure encountered through the subject's confabulation-permeable perception of the multiverse, or both. The subject treats her as real and that is the operationally relevant fact.

**History.** Surfaced during the Sotomayor University arc, Madrimar appears as the formidable matriarch of a lineage of warrior-queens, presented as the subject's grandmother and as a custodian of the heroic tradition the subject understands herself as belonging to. The relationship functions as a *training relationship* with maternal coloration — she is the one adult authority the subject submits to, episodically, for the purpose of skill acquisition and identity ratification.

**Dynamic.** Madrimar is, of all the family figures, the one with whom the subject's behavior most closely resembles ordinary adolescent-coded deference — she shows up, she trains, she chafes, she returns. The chafing is real and so is the return. Madrimar is permitted to give orders the subject would tolerate from no one else. The reason is structural: Madrimar fills, partially, the Elena slot — an older woman whose authority is rooted in demonstrated character and whose pedagogy targets the body, not the affect.

**Trust / safety.** High in the training register, lower in the disclosure register. The subject does not bring her emotional life to Madrimar; she brings her *form*. This is a useful relationship but a partial one, and the subject's instinct to keep it partial is correct — Madrimar is too close to the unprocessed maternal field to be safe for deep disclosure without supervision.

**Failure mode.** The relationship is vulnerable to the same ontological challenge that destabilized the Utopian narrative. If Madrimar is revealed to be wholly confabulatory, the subject loses both a teacher and a piece of internal scaffolding. If Madrimar is revealed to have known of the Washington Heights truth and withheld it, the betrayal would be catastrophic — Madrimar would convert, in the subject's affect, from elder to enemy, with no intermediate stage available to her cognitive style.

**Leverage.** Moderate. Madrimar's endorsement carries weight; her sustained disapproval would produce a behavior change the subject would attribute to her own choice. A hostile actor able to impersonate or coerce Madrimar would gain a brief but high-bandwidth channel of influence before the subject's threat-detection caught up.

---

### 6.5 — THE EDGE LEAGUE / SANTANA APPARATUS — The Procedural "Family" (Negative Origin)

**Status:** Institutional. Personnel partially identified; the apparatus itself is the relevant unit.

**History.** Per *Made in the USA*, the medical-experimental program responsible for the engineering of the subject's powers and, by direct implication, for the conditions under which the Madres were lost. This is family in the negative sense — the body the subject inhabits is, in its capacities, the product of these hands. She did not choose this lineage; it was inscribed in her tissue before she could refuse it.

**Dynamic.** The subject's relationship to the Edge League is the closest thing in her record to *hatred* in the morally organized sense — not the heat of personal grievance but the cold of structural opposition. She does not pursue them with the kinetic frenzy she brings to street-level oppressors; she pursues them, when she pursues them, with a quality of attention she reserves for almost nothing else. This is partly because they are the authors of the unbearable memory her psyche rewrote, and partly because they represent the inverse of her core drive: where she protects the vulnerable, they harvested it.

**Trust / safety.** Zero, structurally. This is one of the few relational fields in the subject's life where her threat-modeling is fully accurate and her response is fully proportionate. There is no avoidance here because there is no ambivalence.

**Failure mode.** The risk is not that the subject will fail to oppose them; the risk is that engagement with the Edge League material will surface the suppressed pediatric-trauma memory at a rate her defenses cannot pace, producing decompensation in operational conditions. She should not pursue this thread without scaffolding; she will pursue it anyway.

**Leverage.** Edge League archival material is the highest-value intelligence asset bearing on the subject's psychology. Custody of it confers, depending on intent, either the capacity to heal her or the capacity to break her.

---

### 6.6 — THE UTOPIAN PARALLEL ITSELF — The Confabulated Homeland as Family-Object

**Status:** Contested ontology. Functionally treated by the subject as natal home and ancestral ground.

**History.** Not a person but, in the subject's psychic economy, a *familial* object — the place that produced her, the lineage she belongs to, the dead she carries. The Parallel is, in object-relations terms, a *holding environment* the subject has internalized in lieu of a continuous family. Its queer-utopian, female-warrior, time-outside-time properties are not incidental; they are the precise inverse of the conditions the subject's actual childhood (per *Made in the USA*) lacked. The Parallel is, in this sense, a *wish* with the structural weight of a memory.

**Dynamic.** The subject draws on the Parallel for replenishment in a way analogous to a person returning to a childhood home. The replenishment is real even if the home is partly imagined — the *function* is operative regardless of the ontology. This is clinically important: the Parallel works *as* a holding environment, and stripping it from her without replacement would be iatrogenic harm.

**Trust / safety.** Total, until challenged. The challenge has already occurred (*Made in the USA*) and the Parallel has survived in her affect with diminished but intact reality-status. This survival is itself diagnostic — the subject is capable of holding contradiction at the affective level even where her cognitive style refuses contradiction at the verbal level.

**Failure mode.** Complete ontological repudiation of the Parallel, particularly if delivered by a trusted source, would remove a structural support the rest of the personality is partly resting on. The subject would survive it but at significant cost. Any intervention should *re-narrate* the Parallel (as inheritance, as aspiration, as the world the Madres would have wanted, as the world Catalina deserves) rather than dissolve it.

**Leverage.** The Parallel is the subject's most intimate non-person attachment. To honor it is to be admitted closer; to mock it is to be excluded permanently and instantly.

---

### 6.7 — SYNTHESIS OF THE FAMILY FIELD

The subject's family architecture is, with the single exception of Catalina, composed of figures who cannot answer back: two dead mothers idealized into structural supports, a grandmother whose ontology is unstable, an institutional enemy that functions as anti-family, and a homeland that may be partly a wish. This composition is not accidental. It is the precise relational ecology an avoidantly-attached, traumatically-bereaved subject would construct if given multiversal means — a family that loves her without demanding presence, that teaches her without requiring disclosure, that hates her without ambivalence, that holds her without confining her.

Catalina is the disruption. Catalina is alive, present, demanding, legitimately aggrieved, and biologically unfalsifiable. The subject's slow, imperfect, non-fleeing engagement with Catalina is the single most important developmental movement in the post-2021 record and the axis along which any future integration of the foundational losses will, if it occurs at all, occur.

The Madres remain the gravitational center. Everything else — the Parallel, Madrimar, the war against the Edge League, even the bond with Catalina — orbits the question the subject has spent her entire published life refusing to ask: *why did they leave me, and was it worth it?* Until that question is permitted to surface, the family field will remain stable, brittle, and incomplete in exactly the configuration documented above.


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

*Cross-reference: §3 Psychological (attachment), §5 Personality (interpersonal pattern). Subject's allies are not a flat list — they are a tiered structure, organized by how much processing they demand of her. The closer a relationship sits to "no processing required," the longer it survives.*

---

## 1. KATE BISHOP — Primary Sustained Attachment

**History.** First substantive contact during the Young Avengers' Mother-arc tour through realities (Gillen, 2013). The bond did not form through shared trauma-talk or team-bonding montage; it formed through shared *operational tempo*. Kate is the only peer who matches the subject's verdict-speed without demanding she narrate the verdict afterward. Continues across *West Coast Avengers* (Thompson, 2018), where the subject relocates to Los Angeles ostensibly to back up Kate's PI work but functionally to be near the one person on Earth whose presence does not raise her cortisol. Periodic appearances since — birthdays, crises, the kind of cameo where the subject portal-arrives with two coffees and no greeting.

**Dynamics.** The relationship operates on a *low-demand, high-availability* protocol. Kate does not text "are you okay?" — she texts the address of a bar. The subject does not reciprocate emotional check-ins; she reciprocates by *appearing* when Kate has been quiet too long. Communication is roughly 70% sarcastic banter, 20% logistics, 10% silence-in-the-same-room. Physical affection is high (arm-slung-over-shoulder, the back-of-the-couch lean, the unselfconscious cuddle pile in *WCA*) and explicitly non-romantic — Kate is straight, the subject is gay, both know it, neither has ever raised it as tension. The platonic boundary is not negotiated; it is climate.

**Evolution.** Began as battlefield trust (Kate's competence registered fast — the subject's threat-pattern-recognition flagged her as *peer, not project* within the first sortie). Deepened in *WCA* through cohabitational proximity — beach house, shared kitchen, shared cases. Has *not* deepened into the kind of intimacy where the subject discusses the Madres. Notably, even in the *Made in the USA* decompensation arc, the subject did not call Kate. This is not distance; it is *category protection* — the Kate-relationship is the one she cannot afford to contaminate with the unprocessed material.

**Trust / Safety Rating.** Highest in subject's life. Kate is the only person the subject would (a) accept tactical orders from without arguing, (b) leave a fight at the request of, (c) admit confusion to, even briefly. Kate is also the only person who can use the subject's first name in a register of softness without producing a flinch-and-deflect.

**Failure Mode.** The relationship would not break through betrayal — Kate is incapable of the relevant betrayals. It would break through *demand*: if Kate ever required the subject to sit still and process, or if Kate were in a crisis that demanded sustained emotional caretaking over weeks, the subject's avoidant architecture would surface — she would arrive, fight the proximate threat, then disappear into another reality "for supplies" and stay gone. Kate, knowing this, has never tested it.

**Leverage.** Anyone who wished to move the subject — for benevolent or hostile reasons — would route through Kate. A credible threat to Kate is the single fastest way to make the subject abandon a current commitment. Conversely, Kate is the only person whose *request* (not order) would cause the subject to attend a thing she does not want to attend. Kate has never weaponized this; the leverage is structural, not exercised.

---

## 2. THE YOUNG AVENGERS COHORT — The First Chosen Team

### 2a. Billy Kaplan (Wiccan)

**History.** Met during Loki's recruitment-by-manipulation phase of *Young Avengers* (Gillen). The subject's initial read of Billy: *soft, reality-warping, dangerous if unsupervised, fundamentally good.* She did not trust the powers; she trusted the conscience under them quickly.

**Dynamics.** A relationship organized around *quiet mutual respect with minimal small talk*. Billy is verbose, processes through dialogue, and is partnered to a man whose love is his stabilizing axis — the subject reads this as the model of a thing she does not have and does not interrogate why. She is protective of Billy in a way she does not announce: she will physically position herself between Billy and incoming ordnance without comment.

**Trust / Safety.** High operational, moderate personal. She would die for him; she would not vacation with him.

**Failure Mode.** Billy's tendency toward reality-rewriting under stress is the latent fracture — the subject's threat-detection would flag a Billy-decompensation event faster than anyone else's, and her response would be to *act* (restrain, displace, portal him out) before he could process her acting. He might experience this as violation. Has not happened in the record; structurally possible.

### 2b. Teddy Altman (Hulkling)

**History.** Co-team member. The subject's relationship with Teddy is the *most uncomplicated team-bond she has* — he is large, kind, competent, and never asks her about her feelings. This is the precise specification of the people she can be around indefinitely.

**Dynamics.** Easy. Banter is light. Teddy is the partner of Billy and his throne-of-the-Kree-Skrull-Empire arc (Ewing, *Empyre*) places him in a leadership tier the subject reflexively respects without being threatened by — because his authority is earned, not titled, and because he never asks her to defer publicly.

**Trust / Safety.** High. She has no defensive posture around Teddy whatsoever — rare datum.

**Failure Mode.** None readily visible. The relationship's only weakness is its low intensity; if Teddy were in catastrophic personal crisis, the subject would *show up* but would not be the right person to *stay*.

### 2c. Tommy Shepherd (Speed)

**History.** Co-team member. The subject reads Tommy as a *fellow restless body* — kinetic discharge as primary affect regulator, mobility as identity. Recognition is mutual and unspoken.

**Dynamics.** Most physical of her team relationships — shoulder-checks, sparring, the kind of banter that escalates to mock-violence and back without anyone reading it as conflict. Of all the Young Avengers, Tommy is the one she would punch in the arm and then buy a slice of pizza for.

**Trust / Safety.** High operational, moderate personal. She trusts his speed in a fight; she does not trust his attention span in a confidence.

**Failure Mode.** Tommy disappears periodically from continuity; she has accepted this without commentary because she does the same.

### 2d. Noh-Varr (Marvel Boy)

**History.** Brief overlap on *Young Avengers*. The subject's read on Noh-Varr was *competent, weird, romantically unserious, not a threat.*

**Dynamics.** Minimal personal investment; tactical respect.

**Trust / Safety.** Operational only.

### 2e. David Alleyne (Prodigy)

**History.** Joined late in *Young Avengers*. The subject's interaction was minimal but cordial. David's omni-knowledge power is precisely the kind of cerebral, processing-heavy presence she does not seek out — there is no hostility, just no orbit.

**Trust / Safety.** Operational only; would respect his read of a situation even when disagreeing.

### 2f. Loki — *catalogued separately under Adversarial Relationships; functionally a teammate during Young Avengers, never an ally.*

---

## 3. THE ULTIMATES (Ewing) — Adult-Tier Operational Family

### 3a. Monica Rambeau (Spectrum)

**History.** Brought onto the Ultimates as the only teen-tier member among cosmic-tier adults. Monica was the de facto field commander.

**Dynamics.** The subject's response to Monica is one of the *rare adult authorities she defers to without resentment* — because Monica is composed, competent, never speaks down, and never demands processing. Monica gave her room; the subject paid it back in obedience-without-comment during operations.

**Trust / Safety.** High operational, moderate personal. The subject would take a tactical order from Monica that she would refuse from any other titled authority.

**Failure Mode.** If Monica ever asked her to *talk about it* in a non-operational moment, the subject would politely, completely, evaporate.

### 3b. Carol Danvers (Captain Marvel)

**History.** Overlap on the Ultimates and surrounding events. Carol is *too much like the subject's brittle-grandiosity register*, and the subject knows it. They are wary of each other in the way two very similar people are wary.

**Dynamics.** Respect, edge, occasional clash. Carol's leadership style during *Civil War II* placed her on a side the subject was uneasy with; the friction is part of the record.

**Trust / Safety.** Operational; personal trust limited by mutual recognition of the same defensive architecture.

**Failure Mode.** Already failed once — the subject left Carol's orbit during/after *CWII* with no announcement. Pattern-typical.

### 3c. Blue Marvel (Adam Brashear) — Mentor-Adjacent

**History.** Ultimates colleague. Adam is a paternal-coded figure: composed, brilliant, principled, old, and *quiet*.

**Dynamics.** The subject's behavior around Adam is the closest she gets to a daughter-around-a-good-father register — slightly more deferential, less performative, listens longer than she does with peers. Notable because she has had so few benevolent older-male figures in her record that the response is novel and visibly works.

**Trust / Safety.** High personal trust for a non-peer; Adam is one of the few adults she'd accept a *correction* from.

**Failure Mode.** Adam asking her, with kindness, what she's running from. She would not have an answer that survived the question. Has not happened.

### 3d. T'Challa, Ms. America — operational, low personal investment.

---

## 4. SOTOMAYOR UNIVERSITY COHORT — The Civilian-Life Experiment

### 4a. Prodigy (David Alleyne, on campus context)

Discussed above. On the Sotomayor campus, briefly her academic-life anchor and confidant — *the closest she came to a sustained college friendship*. Notably, even this relationship occurred within an environment she ultimately fled.

### 4b. Madrimar — *catalogued under §1 Family of Origin; mentor function discussed below.*

### 4c. Magdalena ("Maggie") and the queer-Latina campus social ring

The subject's social experiment at Sotomayor was structured around finding peers who matched her on the *unconflicted* axes (queer, Latina, young, fierce). It worked on those axes. It did not work on the conflicted axis (intimacy). She made friends; she did not make sustained ones. The pattern: warm presence for weeks, then a disappearance "to deal with something off-world," then a reduced-frequency return, then drift. None of the campus relationships are reliable contacts in the current operational period — *all of them lapsed by the subject's withdrawal, not theirs.*

### 4d. Professor Douglas — *adversarial-coded; see Adversarial file.*

---

## 5. MENTORS

### 5a. Storm (Ororo Munroe) — Aspirational Mentor Figure

**History.** Recurrent guest in the subject's solo run. The subject's response to Storm is reverential in a way she shows almost no one else — Storm is the embodiment of the *composed, sovereign, queer-coded-in-the-broad-sense, morally clean, regal-without-being-cold* archetype the subject is trying to grow into.

**Dynamics.** The subject listens to Storm in a register approaching student. She accepts Storm's framing of moments she would not accept from anyone else. This is not because Storm is older or titled — the subject does not respect those — but because Storm models *stillness with power*, the precise thing the subject's architecture has organized itself against and secretly aspires to.

**Trust / Safety.** Very high.

**Failure Mode.** Disappointing Storm. The subject's avoidance of certain conversations is partly the avoidance of having Storm see her unfinished interior.

**Leverage.** Storm's calm direction would move the subject when louder voices would not.

### 5b. The Utopian Warrior Queens (Madrimar's circle / Utopian Parallel matriarchs)

**History.** Encountered during the *America* solo arc when the subject sought training-by-self-exile in the Utopian Parallel.

**Dynamics.** Combat tutors. Ritual elders. Provided the subject with a *cultural-belonging mentor stratum* that the death of the Madres had stripped from her. The relationships are mythically charged — when these figures' historicity is itself revealed (in *Made in the USA*) to be partially confabulated, the subject's grief is for the loss of *mentors who never existed in the form she knew*.

**Trust / Safety.** Was high; is now unstable in the post-retcon period.

**Failure Mode.** The retcon *is* the failure mode — the mentor relationship was foundational and the foundation moved. Subject has not metabolized.

### 5c. Madrimar (Grandmother) — *Family-of-Origin file; also functions as mentor.*

Her arrival in the *America* solo was the closest the subject came to receiving *elder transmission* in canon. The relationship was complicated by the subject's discovery that what Madrimar transmitted was, in part, the curated mythology. The subject's response — characteristic — was not to confront Madrimar but to leave the conversation.

### 5d. Peggy Carter (in the WWII-era / "punch Hitler" sequences)

**History.** Encountered during the subject's recurring time-travel sortie to fight fascists in the 1940s.

**Dynamics.** Mutual recognition of operational style. The subject treats Peggy as a *historical peer* rather than as an elder — a category that suits the subject's allergic relationship to hierarchy. Peggy was one of the few authority-coded figures the subject did not test before deferring to.

**Trust / Safety.** High within the time-displaced context.

**Failure Mode.** The relationship is structurally bounded by its chronological isolation — not a sustainable mentor channel, more a *fortifying ritual* the subject returns to for self-renewal.

---

## 6. PROTÉGÉS / JUNIORS

### 6a. The Teen Brigade (early period, Casey's *Vengeance*)

**History.** First operational team. The subject was a member, not a leader, but functionally took leadership-by-tempo. The Brigade dispersed; the subject did not maintain contacts.

**Dynamics in retrospect.** This was her *first chosen-family experiment* and it followed the template she has repeated since: enter on her terms, lead by acting first, leave without ceremony when the formation no longer suits.

### 6b. Catalina — *Family of Origin file; not protégé.*

### 6c. None sustained.

**This is diagnostic.** A subject this competent and this long-tenured should have accumulated mentees by this point in her career. She has not. The reasons are structural:

1. **Mentorship requires sustained presence.** The subject's avoidant mobility precludes the consistent contact a protégé needs.
2. **Mentorship requires modeling introspection.** The subject does not have the introspective vocabulary to teach what she has not developed.
3. **Mentorship requires admission of one's own learning curve.** The subject's grandiosity-as-armor forecloses the *"I once struggled with this too"* register that a younger person needs to hear.

She is excellent at *interposing for* the vulnerable. She is not, on the current record, equipped to *develop* them.

This is the single largest gap in her relational repertoire and the most likely site of growth in any future arc — the moment a younger powered person attaches to her in earnest will be the moment her defensive architecture is tested in a register it has not yet faced. She cannot punch a teenager who looks up to her, and she cannot leave one who has nowhere else to go, without contradicting the moral spine that organizes her entire personality.

---

## 7. PERIPHERAL ALLY NETWORK — Brief Catalogue

- **Gwenpool:** crossover encounter; the subject's reaction was *bemused-but-tolerant*. Not sustained.
- **Squirrel Girl (Doreen Green):** brief crossover; mutual approval at the operational-warmth level; not sustained.
- **Ms. Marvel (Kamala Khan):** team-up tier; the subject reads Kamala as *protégé-shaped* and has not pursued the relationship for the reasons in §6c above. There is latent potential here that the subject has not activated.
- **She-Hulk:** professional respect; light camaraderie; non-deep.
- **Spider-Gwen / Ghost-Spider:** multiversal acquaintance; mutual respect; no sustained channel.

---

## 8. CROSS-CUTTING PATTERNS

**The "Tempo Test."** Every sustained ally in the subject's life passes a single implicit test: *can you match my decision-tempo without asking me to explain the decision?* Kate passes; Storm passes; Adam Brashear passes (by being unhurried in a way that does not slow others). Lisa Halloran failed; the Sotomayor friends failed; Loki actively gamed the test.

**The "Stillness Allergy."** Every relationship that demands the subject sit in a room and feel a thing will, eventually, lose her. The only relationships that survive are those that permit her to *move through* the room while loving the person in it. Kate built her friendship on this principle. Storm operates by it. Adam Brashear allows it. The Madres, in her memory, never required otherwise.

**The "Category Protection" Pattern.** The subject's closest people are *protected from* her trauma material, not *trusted with* it. This is a counter-intuitive datum. The conventional model assumes intimacy = disclosure. The subject's model is: *I love you, therefore I will not contaminate you with what I have not metabolized.* This is both a defense and a perverse kindness, and it is the single hardest thing about her to read correctly from the outside.

**Aggregate Leverage Map.** In descending order, the contacts whose *peril* would re-route the subject from any current commitment: Kate Bishop → Madrimar (despite the unresolved retcon) → Catalina → Billy & Teddy (jointly) → Storm → Monica Rambeau → Adam Brashear. The contacts whose *request* would draw her into a thing she does not want to do: Kate → Storm → Adam → Monica. The contacts whose *disapproval* would unsettle her: Storm → Adam → Madrimar → Kate.

**Final note for the file.** The subject's allies are fewer than her tenure and profile would predict, but each is selected with precision for the demand-profile she can sustain. She is not lonely in the conventional sense; she is *load-balanced* — distributing affection across enough relationships, each calibrated to her tolerance, that none individually approaches the demand a true single intimacy would impose. This works. It works the way a successful avoidant system always works: at the cost of the depth that the structure exists to prevent.


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

*Dossier Section 7.3. Continues from §7.1 (Family of Origin) and §7.2 (Peers & Team Affiliations). This section maps adversarial and intimate dyads — the people the subject has wanted to destroy, the people who have wanted to destroy her, and the people she has let inside the perimeter. The categories braid: in the subject's life, "rival" frequently bleeds into "lover" via competitive admiration, and "enemy" frequently bleeds into "mirror" via shared trauma vocabulary. Each dyad below is mapped on six axes — history, dynamics, evolution, trust/safety, failure mode, leverage — per file convention.*

---

## A. RIVALS

### A.1 Loki Laufeyson

**History.** First sustained contact: *Young Avengers* (Gillen, 2013), Loki embedded as a kid-form god on a team the subject had already half-joined and half-rejected. The pre-history is structural rather than personal — the subject had no prior beef with Loki; she walked into the room and read him on sight. Her opening operational decision toward him was to punch him through a series of dimensional walls, a greeting unprecedented in her record toward any other teammate.

**Dynamics.** Loki is the single most diagnostically useful relationship in the subject's adversarial file because he is the inverse of her on nearly every behavioral axis. He is verbal where she is kinetic, manipulative where she is declarative, identity-fluid where she is identity-stable, and inheritance-bound where she is self-made. Her hostility toward him is not strategic threat-assessment so much as somatic revulsion — he activates every defense in her stack simultaneously. He represents *narrative that cannot be trusted*, and the subject's entire self-organization rests on a narrative she has chosen not to interrogate; his presence is therefore destabilizing at the foundational level, and she manages the destabilization the only way she knows how, with her legs.

**Evolution.** The dynamic does not soften. Even after Loki's partial rehabilitation arc within the team, the subject's posture toward him remains pre-emptive contempt. She is, however, observed to *use* him — Loki is the only teammate she will deploy as a tool while openly disavowing him as a person, which is a managerial style she does not employ elsewhere. By the late *Young Avengers* run, the relationship has stabilized into a kind of operational tolerance: he is permitted in the room, he is never permitted near her back. In subsequent appearances she does not seek him out and does not avoid him; if he is present she treats him as terrain hazard.

**Trust / Safety.** Trust is zero and stable at zero. Crucially, this is the most *psychologically safe* low-trust relationship in her file — she does not have to negotiate her distrust, manage his feelings about it, or worry that her distrust will damage him. He has earned it and accepts the assignment. There is a perverse comfort in the dyad: a relationship in which her defenses are not pathologized.

**Failure mode.** She underestimates him by overestimating her ability to detect him. Her counterphobic confidence ("I see him coming") is occasionally wrong in narrow technical ways; Loki's manipulations of the broader Young Avengers team succeeded in part because she trusted her threat-read and disengaged from group-level vigilance once she had clocked him. The failure mode is: she will catch him in the obvious lie and miss the structural one.

**Leverage.** She holds the leverage. He cannot manipulate her via emotion (she does not extend him any), via narrative (she refuses his stories), or via team-loyalty appeals (her loyalty to him is null). The only leverage he has ever exerted on her was via threat to people she does protect — and even then she responds with force, not negotiation. He, conversely, is leveraged by her in any room they share simply by her willingness to put him through a wall on probability rather than evidence.

---

### A.2 Kate Bishop (Rivalry-Sublimated-Into-Bond)

*Cross-referenced from §7.2; included here because the file would be incomplete without the rivalry vector.*

**History.** Co-membership on Young Avengers; later overlapping operational sphere via West Coast Avengers. The competitive substrate is constant: both are non-powered-equivalent (Kate) and powered (the subject) peer-leaders of the same micro-generation, both code as "the competent one," both have a swagger register, both are mistrustful of authority.

**Dynamics.** What in any other dyad would have calcified into rivalry sublimates here into the closest sustained attachment in the subject's file. The mechanism is Kate's specific style of acceptance: she meets the swagger without competing for it and without trying to dismantle it. The subject's standard rival-trigger (peer of comparable competence) is disarmed by Kate's refusal to play the dominance game. The result is the only relationship in which the subject sustains intimacy without exit behavior.

**Evolution / Trust / Failure / Leverage.** See §7.2.A.1. Noted here only to mark: in the absence of Kate's specific disarming style, this would have been the subject's most dangerous rival relationship, not her most stable friendship. The dyad is a counterfactual lesson in how thin the line is, for this subject, between best friend and adversary.

---

### A.3 The Warrior Queens of the Utopian Parallel (Queen-Mother-Figures / Training Rivals)

**History.** Encountered across *Young Avengers* coda and developed in *America* (Rivera, 2017). The Queens — particularly the matriarchal command of the Parallel — function simultaneously as cultural homeland, training cadre, and mythic mother-substitutes. The subject leaves Sotomayor University repeatedly to train with them; this is presented in the text as cultural pilgrimage and operates psychologically as displacement of unmet maternal need onto a glamorous, undemanding surrogate.

**Dynamics.** The rivalry register is competitive-apprentice: the subject is *almost* their equal but not quite, and the gap is the engine of return. They demand from her physically without demanding from her emotionally — the ideal training relationship for a subject whose somatic vocabulary is fluent and whose affective vocabulary is not. They are also implicated in the *Made in the USA* destabilization: when the Utopian narrative itself is called into question, the Queens' status as legitimate cultural authority is silently compromised. The subject does not address this directly in the record.

**Evolution.** Idealized in the *Young Avengers* era; functional-but-fraught through *America*; markedly less foregrounded after *Made in the USA*. The withdrawal is not explicit; it is the absence of return, which is the subject's standard exit signature.

**Trust / Safety.** High trust in the operational register, brittle trust in the narrative register. They are safe to spar with, unsafe to question.

**Failure mode.** The subject uses the Queens as a place to *go to* rather than a place to *be from*. They are scaffolding for the avoidance, not a resolution of it.

**Leverage.** They hold significant leverage by holding the keys to the homeland narrative. After *Made in the USA*, that leverage is compromised but not nullified — the subject can no longer fully believe them, but she has not built an alternative cultural home, so the door stays cracked.

---

### A.4 The Exterminatrix / La Legion (Operational Rivals)

**History.** Antagonists across *America* run. The Exterminatrix arc establishes a recurring pattern: the subject acquires an antagonist who functions as a peer-aggressor — comparable strength, comparable willingness to escalate, ideological opposition.

**Dynamics.** These rivals are *uncomplicated* in the file. They escalate, she escalates harder, the matter is resolved kinetically. The diagnostic value is in what they *don't* trigger: no destabilization, no exit behavior, no narrative threat. They are exactly the kind of opposition her system is built to handle and they confirm by contrast which rivals (Loki, the Queens, the *Made in the USA* revelations) are dangerous to her in ways punching cannot resolve.

**Evolution.** Cyclical. Defeat, return, defeat, return. No sustained development arc.

**Trust / Safety / Failure / Leverage.** Trust nil, safety high (because predictable), failure mode minimal, leverage low in both directions. These are the rivals she enjoys.

---

## B. ENEMIES

### B.1 The Santana Procedure / The Edge League (Pediatric-Medical Antagonist Complex)

**History.** Revealed in *Made in the USA* (Vazquez, 2021) as the buried-origin engine of her powers and a foundational trauma source. The Edge League conducted experimental procedures on her in early childhood in Washington Heights; the Utopian narrative was, per this revision, generated as a protective overlay against the unbearable memory.

**Dynamics.** This is not an enemy she can punch in the conventional sense, which is precisely why it is the most dangerous entry in her enemies file. The opposition is *to her memory itself* — the people responsible are partly past, partly present, and partly inside her own neurology in the form of the somatic engineering they performed. The dyad is structurally asymmetrical: they have shaped her body and her story; she can only retroactively contest both.

**Evolution.** Pre-discovery: zero conscious relationship; the enemy was operating beneath the level of awareness, having installed a comforting fiction in lieu of the true memory. Post-discovery: brief dissociative episode, then her standard re-stabilization through action, then a pursuit arc that gives the file its most behaviorally honest sequence — the subject hunting the people who hurt the child she had not let herself remember being.

**Trust / Safety.** Trust nil; safety actively negative. The Edge League is the only enemy in the file with the demonstrated capacity to rewrite her interior, and that capacity, once exercised, cannot be guaranteed expended.

**Failure mode.** Her standard tool-set (kinetic discharge, geographic exit, narrative override) is *the symptom of the injury they inflicted*. Every reflex she has for managing them was shaped by them. She cannot fight this enemy purely on her own resources without re-enacting their work; resolution requires the introspective infrastructure she has spent her life avoiding building.

**Leverage.** They hold the highest leverage of any entity in the file — they can, in principle, destabilize her foundational narrative on cue. The subject's only counter-leverage is *refusal to be destabilized*, which is itself a form of the original defense. The standoff is, in the deepest sense, unresolved.

---

### B.2 Mother (the Young Avengers' interdimensional parental antagonist)

**History.** Series-spanning antagonist of *Young Avengers* (Gillen). A parasitic entity feeding on young heroes by exploiting parental archetypes.

**Dynamics.** For a subject whose central wound is maternal sacrifice/abandonment, an antagonist literally named Mother who weaponizes parent-figure templates is so on-the-nose that the file marks it as overdetermined. The subject's behavior in the arc is illustrative: she does not engage Mother psychologically, will not banter, will not be drawn into the parental dynamic the entity is offering. She treats Mother as a problem of geometry — find the portal, close the portal, exit the reality. This is *appropriate tactical response* and also *defensive refusal of the symbolic content*.

**Evolution.** Antagonist resolved within arc; the dynamic is single-arc but psychologically signal.

**Trust / Safety.** Trust nil. Safety, notably, *higher than expected* — the subject is less destabilized by Mother than by Loki, because Mother's threat is external and physical while Loki's is narrative and internal. Mother she can kick.

**Failure mode.** Refusal to engage the symbolic content meant she did not work through anything; the antagonist was defeated without the subject having to feel anything about being targeted as someone with a maternal wound. Operationally successful, psychologically wasted opportunity.

**Leverage.** Mother's leverage was archetypal and the subject denied it traction by refusing to participate in the archetype. This is one of the cleaner demonstrations in the file of her primary defense working *correctly* — the kinetic-action response as genuine survival strategy, not merely as avoidance.

---

### B.3 Hitler (and the broader category of *Historical Evil as Punching Bag*)

**History.** Running gag-or-not-a-gag through *America*: the subject leaves campus, leaves the timeline, locates Hitler, punches Hitler, returns. The trope-detail is so frequently repeated it functions as a behavioral marker.

**Dynamics.** This entry is filed under Enemies because the action is real (within the fiction) and because the *category* of opposition — historical perpetrators of mass harm — is genuinely the subject's enemy in her moral universe. But the operational function is regulatory: when affect rises, she finds a deserving target across time and discharges. The enemy here is partly Hitler and partly her own nervous system; punching the former regulates the latter.

**Evolution.** Constant frequency, stable across runs. Never depicted as personally costly, never produces lingering injury, never escalates into a sustained arc.

**Trust / Safety.** N/A in conventional terms. Safety-relevant detail: this is one of the few enemy-classes she engages without any destabilization risk, because the moral clarity is total and the encounter is brief.

**Failure mode.** The activity is a perfect closed loop of moral satisfaction plus somatic discharge, which is *exactly* the kind of activity that forecloses the slower work she does not want to do. It is the most efficient possible avoidance ritual.

**Leverage.** None either way. The category is leverage-inert, which is part of its appeal to her.

---

### B.4 Generalized Oppressor / Bigot Class (Recurring Adversary Type)

**History.** Threaded throughout *America* and later appearances: landlords, ICE-analog figures, harassers in bars, anti-queer street violence. These are not single antagonists but a *class*, and the subject's response to them is uniform.

**Dynamics.** This is where the subject is most morally legible and least psychologically defended. She does not need to manage anything; the response is immediate, proportional-to-disproportional, and uncomplicated by ambivalence. The dyad is one-directional — they offend, she intervenes, done.

**Evolution.** None required. The class is recurrent; the response is constant.

**Trust / Safety.** Trust nil, safety irrelevant; the dyad does not penetrate her perimeter.

**Failure mode.** Risk of overreach — she will intervene without consultation with the victim, which can occasionally produce paternalism in tension with her stated values. The record shows occasional course-correction when called on this by community members; she takes the correction better here than in nearly any other context, because it aligns with her moral spine.

**Leverage.** None toward her. She holds total leverage in these dyads and exercises it openly.

---

### B.5 Her Own Forgotten Childhood Self (Internal Enemy)

**History.** This is a meta-entry but the file requires it. Per the *Made in the USA* record, the most persistent adversarial relationship the subject maintains is with the child she was — the medical-trauma subject in Washington Heights whom the Utopian narrative was constructed to bury.

**Dynamics.** The relationship is denial-and-displacement on her side; the buried self exerts pressure through dissociative episodes, restlessness, refusal of stillness, somatic vigilance, and the entire architecture of her defenses. Every avoidance behavior in the file is, viewed from this angle, a sustained refusal to be in the same room with this child.

**Evolution.** Pre-*Made in the USA*: total suppression. Post-discovery: partial acknowledgment, then re-suppression via action. The integration work is not done in the published record.

**Trust / Safety.** The subject does not trust her own memory and has good reason not to; safety is destabilized whenever the buried material approaches consciousness.

**Failure mode.** Untreated, the internal enemy *is* the personality structure — there is no path to full functioning that does not route through reconciliation with this self. The subject's current trajectory routes around it.

**Leverage.** Total. This is the entity with the most leverage over the subject in the entire file, and the subject is aware of it at the level of behavior even where she is not at the level of language.

---

### B.6 Catalina (Sister) — Liminal Entry Between Enemy and Family

*Primary file: §7.1.* Cross-referenced here because in the *Made in the USA* arc Catalina occupies an adversarial position before resolving toward kin. The subject's initial response to a sibling she did not know existed is hostility, suspicion of fabrication, and an exit attempt — all consistent with her standard defense set when the foundational narrative is challenged. The eventual reframing toward sister-kin is incomplete in the published record and is one of the file's most important open relationships.

---

## C. LOVERS & INTIMATES

### C.1 Lisa Halloran

**History.** Sotomayor University girlfriend, *America* (Rivera, 2017). The relationship is the most sustained romantic dyad in the published record and the single richest behavioral source on the subject's intimate-relational pattern.

**Dynamics.** Lisa is depicted as grounded, present, available — the partner equivalent of the academic environment the subject was attempting and failing to occupy. She is what the subject thinks she wants (normative young-adult life, queer domesticity, stability) and structurally what the subject cannot tolerate (sustained proximity, expectation of return, the requirement that the subject *be where she said she would be*). The mismatch is not about Lisa's qualities; Lisa is, on the page, eminently lovable. The mismatch is about the subject's incapacity to remain.

**Evolution.** Initial enthusiasm — the subject pursues, the subject commits, the subject performs partnership. Mid-arc friction — she leaves to punch Hitler, to train with the Queens, to handle a crisis; she returns; she leaves again. Lisa's complaints are reasonable and the subject hears them as captivity. Late-arc dissolution — not via a single rupture but via accumulated absence; the relationship ends in the manner the subject's relationships generally end, by her not being there.

**Trust / Safety.** Lisa offered high trust and emotional safety; the subject could not metabolize the offer. The failure was not in the safety provided but in the subject's nervous system's inability to recognize safety as safety rather than as enclosure.

**Failure mode.** This is the file's clearest example of the *deactivation* pattern. The subject did not stop loving Lisa; she activated her exit-architecture in response to the closeness *because* she was loving her. The relationship failed at exactly the depth at which she could not breathe.

**Leverage.** Lisa held leverage only by virtue of mattering, which the subject managed by reducing the mattering through distance. There is no record of Lisa attempting to exploit the leverage; she asked for ordinary presence and received intermittent absence.

**Open question.** The file flags this relationship as a potential return-point. Should the subject undertake the integration work outlined in §3 and §4, Lisa (or a successor partner of similar register) is the most likely site of either repair or repetition. The current trajectory predicts repetition; the latent capacity predicts repair.

---

### C.2 Kate Bishop (Non-Romantic Intimate)

*Cross-referenced from §7.2 and §A.2 above.* Filed here under intimates because in the subject's actual relational architecture, Kate occupies the slot a long-term primary partner would in a more conventionally organized adult — the trusted person, the not-negotiated bond, the person from whom she does not need to flee. The subject is not romantically involved with Kate. The intimate-relational function is nonetheless performed by Kate more reliably than by any romantic partner in the file. This is diagnostic: the subject can sustain intimacy when the genital/erotic register is *off the table*, because the erotic register activates the maternal-loss substrate (the Madres were the original lost loves) and triggers the exit reflex. Friendship operates beneath that activation threshold and is therefore survivable.

---

### C.3 Pre-Lisa / Inferred Prior Partners

The record implies, without depicting in detail, prior relationships during the Teen Brigade / early Young Avengers era. The behavioral baseline established by Lisa suggests these were brief, kinetic, exit-managed, and unremembered with regret. The subject does not appear to carry torch-bearing nostalgia for any previous partner, which is itself a data point — either the relationships were too shallow to imprint, or the imprinting was managed by the same memory-organization processes that handled the Utopian confabulation. The file marks this as low-resolution but probable.

---

### C.4 The Madres (Mami and Amalia / the lost-parent objects, eroticized only in the displaced sense of *first love*)

*Primary file: §7.1.* Noted here because in the subject's intimate-relational architecture, the Madres are the original lost loves and every subsequent intimate is, structurally, recruited to replace them and tested for the capacity to leave. The displacement is non-erotic in content but governs the erotic field by setting its rules: *the person I love most will choose to leave me, heroically, with my approval, and I will be alone.* The subject's exit reflex is, in this reading, a pre-emptive inhabitation of the Madres' position — she leaves first to avoid being the one left.

---

### C.5 The Utopian Parallel (As Eroticized Object / Homeland-Lover)

The file notes, with appropriate caution, that the subject's relationship to the Utopian Parallel itself carries intimate-register affect — longing, idealization, return-fantasy, the description of its women in terms that braid cultural reverence with something approaching romantic awe. The Parallel functions as a *homeland-lover*, a place that holds her in the way a partner might. After the *Made in the USA* destabilization, this relationship enters the same category as her relationship with the Madres' narrative: cherished, compromised, unresolved, and still operative at the level of longing even where it has been called into question at the level of fact.

---

## D. CROSS-DYAD SYNTHESIS

Three patterns emerge across the rivals/enemies/lovers field:

**First**, the subject is *most stable* in relationships where the other party makes no claim on her interiority — Kate (no claim by style), Loki (no claim by mutual contempt), the Exterminatrix-class adversaries (no claim by category), Hitler-class targets (no claim by moral asymmetry). She is *least stable* in relationships where claims on her interiority are made gently and legitimately: Lisa, the Queens after destabilization, Catalina, and her own buried self. The pattern is not "she cannot do closeness." The pattern is "she cannot do closeness that asks her to know herself."

**Second**, her enemies are organized along a hidden axis: those who attack her body (the Exterminatrix, generalized oppressor class, Mother) versus those who attack her narrative (Loki, the Edge League, the implications of *Made in the USA*, her own buried self). She is built for the first category and unbuilt for the second. The most dangerous figures in her file are not the strongest; they are the ones whose threat is epistemic.

**Third**, the rivals/enemies/lovers categories are *not stable* in her life — they translate into each other. Kate is a rivalry that became kinship. Catalina is family that arrived as enemy. The Madres are k


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION: POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS

## Subject: America Chavez / "Miss America"

---

## 6.1 Preamble: Why the Power Map Is Also a Psychological Map

A complete inventory of this subject's capabilities is not separable from a complete inventory of her defenses. Where most powered subjects manifest abilities that are *adjacent* to their psychology — a flight power expressing freedom, a healing power expressing care — this subject's power-set is *isomorphic* to her defense structure. She does not have powers that happen to suit her psychology; she has a psychology that has been organized around what her body can do, and a body that has been engineered (per *Made in the USA*) to do what her psychology requires. Strength absorbs blows that would otherwise demand grief. Invulnerability removes the convalescent state in which trauma would have to be metabolized. Flight removes the constraint of terrain. The portal kick removes the constraint of reality itself. Every capacity is a route out of stillness, which is the only state she cannot survive.

The file therefore proceeds capability-by-capability with the dual reading: mechanism *and* signature.

---

## 6.2 Class-Tier Strength

**Mechanism.** Per consistent canonical depiction across *Vengeance* (2011), *Young Avengers* (2013), *Ultimates* / *Ultimates²* (Ewing, 2015–2017), *America* (Rivera, 2017–2018), *West Coast Avengers* (Thompson, 2018), and *Made in the USA* (Vazquez, 2021), the subject operates at the upper tier of unaugmented physical strength in the Marvel field — credibly trading blows with Thor-equivalents in *Ultimates*, dismantling a Celestial-tier construct from the inside (*Ultimates²* #100), and routinely shattering vibranium-grade restraints without specialized technique. There is no canonical upper bound established by failure; she has never been depicted as out-lifted.

**Range and modulation.** What separates her from most strength-tier operators is the *fineness* of modulation. She can pick up Kate Bishop without bruising her; she can throw an opponent across a city block; she can apply just enough force to a door to break the lock without removing the door from the frame. The modulation is fluent and unconscious — a developmental fact, not a learned restraint, suggesting the strength came online early enough to be integrated into baseline motor learning rather than acquired adult-onset.

**Growth over time.** The published record does not show a strength curve; she is presented at ceiling from her first appearance. What *does* curve is her *willingness* to deploy ceiling-level force. *Vengeance*-era subject hits to disable; *Young Avengers*-era subject hits to make a point (Loki, repeatedly, through realities); *Ultimates*-era subject hits to solve cosmological problems; *America*-era subject pulls strikes more often, having begun — briefly, partially — to consider consequence. *Made in the USA*-era subject reverts: when destabilized, the modulation coarsens.

**Signature applications.** The downward axe-handle strike (both fists, full body weight, near-vertical descent) when a fight needs to end. The single-arm shove that doubles as a portal-launch (see §6.5). The horizontal forearm clothesline she uses when she wants to humiliate rather than damage.

**Symptom-as-signature.** Strength this controlled and this rarely tested at its ceiling is, paradoxically, a *containment* power. The story she tells herself with it is *I cannot be moved.* This is psychologically necessary: a child who has been physically removed from her parents (or her parents from her) by forces she could not resist must, as an adult, organize her body around the fact that no force can move her again. The strength is not for hitting; it is for *not being relocated*. The hitting is incidental.

---

## 6.3 Durability / Near-Invulnerability

**Mechanism.** Subdermal density and tensile properties on the order of secondary-Avenger tier; canonical resistance to small-arms fire, energy weapons of mid-tier yield, falls from orbital height (*America* #1, the entry sequence), and direct contact with cosmic-scale entities (*Ultimates²*). The *Made in the USA* retcon attributes the engineered substrate to the Santana procedure — the body was *made* to take impact, which is congruent with the procedure's pediatric origin (a child built into an instrument).

**Range and limits.** Documented limits are narrow but real. Magical / reality-warping attacks bypass the durability — Loki's interventions in *Young Avengers* land emotionally because they cannot be tanked physically. Sufficient cosmic-tier ordnance (Celestial-class) registers as injury. Restraint by reality-anchoring fields (the binding sequences in *Made in the USA*) holds her, which is significant: she is not invulnerable to *being held*, only to being damaged. The distinction matters; see §6.7.

**Growth over time.** No clear durability arc. What evolves is her *relationship to injury* — early-era she ignores wounds because she heals fast; mid-era she ignores them because that is the role; late-era (*Made in the USA*) she ignores them in ways that read as dissociative rather than confident.

**Signature applications.** Walking *into* attacks rather than around them. Standing in front of a blast aimed at a teammate without first calculating whether she can absorb it. Re-entering atmosphere unprotected.

**Symptom-as-signature.** This is the most diagnostically loud of her powers. A subject who never convalesces never sits with what was done to her. The durability is, in clinical terms, a *prosthetic for the absent capacity to be hurt and recover* — which is to say, the absent capacity to grieve. The file notes (§2) that her injuries resolve off-panel; this is structurally consistent. She does not have a recovery sequence because recovery is the psychological territory she cannot enter. Her body has been engineered to spare her from the experience that would force her into it.

---

## 6.4 Flight

**Mechanism.** Self-propelled atmospheric and exoatmospheric flight; no visible thrust mechanism, no observed aerodynamic dependency. Vacuum-survivable for at least the duration of inter-orbital transit (*Ultimates*). Top speeds are inconsistently rendered but credibly transonic in atmosphere and apparently FTL-equivalent when paired with portal traversal across cosmological distances.

**Range and limits.** Limited only by her need to breathe in unsuitable environments — she does not appear to require atmosphere for short durations but has been depicted gasping after extended vacuum exposure. Cannot, apparently, fly *through* solid mass (which is what the portal capacity is for).

**Growth over time.** The interesting curve here is not capacity but *posture*. Early-era flight posture is forward-leaning, fist-first, projectile-style. Mid-era, especially in Rivera's *America*, the posture relaxes — she will fly seated, arms crossed, leaning back, conversational. Late-era reverts to combat posture under stress. The posture is a stress index.

**Signature applications.** The hover-and-cross-arms, used as a power-display stance when she wants negotiation to end and compliance to begin. The straight-line ascent-through-ceiling, used as exit. The carry — she will pick up a non-flying teammate and transit without announcing the intent, which is partly tactical and partly her aversion to discussing the obvious.

**Symptom-as-signature.** Flight is freedom from terrain, and terrain is the medium of *being followed*.
